240 if (this.registered.length === this.scripts.length) {

241 this.registered.forEach(function (fn) {

242 if (typeof fn === 'function') {

243 setTimeout(fn, 0);

244 }

245 });

246 this.ready = function () {};

247 }

248 },

249

250 insert: function (s) {

251 var t = d.getElementById('js-position' + this.index);

252 if (t && t.insertAdjacentElement) {

253 t.insertAdjacentElement('afterend', s);

254 } else {

255 d.head.appendChild(s);

256 }

257 ++this.index;

258 },

259

260 createScript: function (script, beforeLoad) {

261 var s = d.createElement('script');

262 s.id = 'js-position' + (this.index + 1);

263 s.setAttribute('data-test', script.test);

264 if (beforeLoad) {

265 s.defer = 'defer';

266 s.onload = function () {

267 if (script.noinit) {

268 loader.register(true);

269 }

270 if (d.readyState === 'interactive' || d.readyState === 'complete') {

271 loader.ready();

272 }

273 };

274 } else {

275 s.async = 'async';

276 }

277 s.src = script.src;

278 return s;

279 },

280

281 init: function () {

282 this.scripts.forEach(function (s) {

283 loader.insert(loader.createScript(s, true));

284 });

285

286 d.addEventListener('DOMContentLoaded', function () {

287 loader.ready();

288

289 var conditionalScripts = [

290 {match: 'div[data-pan-container]', src: '/static/js/pan-zoom-es6-bundle-464a2af269.js', test: 'pan-zoom-js', module: true },

291 {match: 'div[data-pan-container]', src: '/static/js/pan-zoom-es5-bundle-2626f1bdf8.js', test: 'pan-zoom-js', nomodule: true },

292 {match: 'math,span.mathjax-tex', src: '/static/js/math-es6-bundle-d616f8e4f9.js', test: 'math-js', module: true},

293 {match: 'math,span.mathjax-tex', src: '/static/js/math-es5-bundle-66109c5184.js', test: 'math-js', nomodule: true}

294 ];

295

296

297 if (conditionalScripts) {

298 conditionalScripts.filter(function (script) {

299 return !!document.querySelector(script.match) && !((moduleSupport && script.nomodule) || (!moduleSupport && script.module));

300 }).forEach(function (script) {

301 loader.insert(loader.createScript(script));

302 });

303 }

304 }, false);

305 }

306 };

307 loader.init();

308 }

309 })(window, document);

310</script>

356 <meta name="dc.description" content="Haematopoietic stem cells (HSCs) home to the bone marrow via, in part, interactions with vascular cell adhesion molecule-1 (VCAM1)1&#8211;3. Once in the bone marrow, HSCs are vetted by perivascular phagocytes to ensure their self-integrity. Here we show that VCAM1 is also expressed on healthy HSCs and upregulated on leukaemic stem cells (LSCs), where it serves as a quality-control checkpoint for entry into bone marrow by providing &#8216;don&#8217;t-eat-me&#8217; stamping in the context of major histocompatibility complex class-I (MHC-I) presentation. Although haplotype-mismatched HSCs can engraft, Vcam1 deletion, in the setting of haplotype mismatch, leads to impaired haematopoietic recovery due to HSC clearance by mononuclear phagocytes. Mechanistically, VCAM1 &#8216;don&#8217;t-eat-me&#8217; activity is regulated by &#946;2-microglobulin MHC presentation on HSCs and paired Ig-like receptor-B (PIR-B) on phagocytes. VCAM1 is also used by cancer cells to escape immune detection as its expression is upregulated in multiple cancers, including acute myeloid leukaemia (AML), where high expression associates with poor prognosis. In AML, VCAM1 promotes disease progression, whereas VCAM1 inhibition or deletion reduces leukaemia burden and extends survival. These results suggest that VCAM1 engagement regulates a critical immune-checkpoint gate in the bone marrow, and offers an alternative strategy to eliminate cancer cells via modulation of the innate immune tolerance. Pinho et al. show that VCAM1 and MHC-I cooperate to provide a &#8216;don&#8217;t-eat-me&#8217; signal that prevents haematopoietic stem cells clearance by mononuclear phagocytes, and also that VCAM1 can be hijacked by cancer cells to escape innate immune surveillance."/>

825 <section aria-labelledby="Abs1" data-title="Abstract" lang="en"><div class="c-article-section" id="Abs1-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Abs1">Abstract</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Abs1-content"><p>Haematopoietic stem cells (HSCs) home to the bone marrow via, in part, interactions with vascular cell adhesion molecule-1 (VCAM1)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Miyake, K. et al. A VCAM-like adhesion molecule on murine bone marrow stromal cells mediates binding of lymphocyte precursors in culture. J. Cell Biol. 114, 557‚Äì565 (1991)." href="#ref-CR1" id="ref-link-section-d21779968e682">1</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Simmons, P. J. et al. Vascular cell adhesion molecule-1 expressed by bone marrow stromal cells mediates the binding of hematopoietic progenitor cells. Blood 80, 388‚Äì395 (1992)." href="#ref-CR2" id="ref-link-section-d21779968e682_1">2</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 3" title="Ulyanova, T. et al. VCAM-1 expression in adult hematopoietic and nonhematopoietic cells is controlled by tissue-inductive signals and reflects their developmental origin. Blood 106, 86‚Äì94 (2005)." href="/articles/s41556-022-00849-4#ref-CR3" id="ref-link-section-d21779968e685">3</a></sup>. Once in the bone marrow, HSCs are vetted by perivascular phagocytes to ensure their self-integrity. Here we show that VCAM1 is also expressed on healthy HSCs and upregulated on leukaemic stem cells (LSCs), where it serves as a quality-control checkpoint for entry into bone marrow by providing ‚Äòdon‚Äôt-eat-me‚Äô stamping in the context of major histocompatibility complex class-I (MHC-I) presentation. Although haplotype-mismatched HSCs can engraft, <i>Vcam1</i> deletion, in the setting of haplotype mismatch, leads to impaired haematopoietic recovery due to HSC clearance by mononuclear phagocytes. Mechanistically, VCAM1 ‚Äòdon‚Äôt-eat-me‚Äô activity is regulated by Œ≤2-microglobulin MHC presentation on HSCs and paired Ig-like receptor-B (PIR-B) on phagocytes. VCAM1 is also used by cancer cells to escape immune detection as its expression is upregulated in multiple cancers, including acute myeloid leukaemia (AML), where high expression associates with poor prognosis. In AML, VCAM1 promotes disease progression, whereas VCAM1 inhibition or deletion reduces leukaemia burden and extends survival. These results suggest that VCAM1 engagement regulates a critical immune-checkpoint gate in the bone marrow, and offers an alternative strategy to eliminate cancer cells via modulation of the innate immune tolerance.</p></div></div></section>

Values were normalized to the maximum number of events measured across technical replicates (n‚Äâ=‚Äâ6). Error bars, mean ¬± s.e.m. Box plots: media, whiskers: minimum and maximum. Two-way ANOVA with multiple comparisons correction (<b>j</b>). ns, non-significant. Significant <i>P</i> values are indicated in the figure.</p><p>

1379 <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41556-022-00849-4#MOESM15">Source data</a>

(<b>a</b>) VCAM1 is broadly expressed across all FAB AML subgroups with the highest expression on the M6 subgroup. (<b>b</b>) Association between VCAM1 expression and human AML mutations.
